Having completed this book for you, my sons, the last of the knowledge in medicine with its complement, and having reached an end to it through explanations of it and declarations thereof, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you along with this Treatise which is part of the operation, namely surgery with one's hand.
Since the operation with the hand is utterly private in our region and in our time, and perhaps the knowledge of it has perished and its trail has been lost, and there have not remained from it except small descriptions in old books which hands have altered and into which error and hesitation have occurred until their intentions were closed up and their force was weakened. It seemed to me that I should bring it back to life along with the arrangement of this Treatise by way of its position, declaration, and abbreviation: and that I should be reconciled with the forms of iron instruments, cautery, and other tools of the operation with the addition of explanation and the necessity for them.
However, the reason why a good craftsman of it with his own hand is not found in this our time, is: because the art of medicine is long and its author must be exercised beforehand in the science of anatomy which Galen narrated, until he knows the remedies for limbs, and their forms, and their connections, and separations, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, tendons, and their numbers, and their exit and entry, and places of exit of arteries, pulsating and quiet, and outlets.
And for this reason Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, but with work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
But we have already spoken of him at the entrance to this book.
Since he who is not knowing what we have said about anatomy is not purged, lest he already falls into error by which men are destroyed: just as I have seen many of those who are formed from this science and boast of it without knowledge and without experience.
What happened was that I saw a foolish doctor cut an apse of elephantiasis on the throat of a woman, and he struck some arteries in the throat; why the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead between his hands.
And I saw another doctor who supposed to draw out a stone from a man, who was advanced in age, and the stone was great. Therefore he came to him and drew it out along with a piece of the bladder. Why the man died on the third day.
And I myself had been called to draw it out, and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the patient that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was taking a fee from one of the Dukes of our land on account of medicine: and he happened to an eunuch black man who was with him, breaking in his leg near the heel: and the doctor hurried with his ignorance, and compressed the fracture over the wound with poultices and bandages tightly bound, and did not let out any breathing from the wound.
Then he left him according to his desires. Then he dismissed him after a few days, and commanded him not to untie the bandage: and he stood thus until his leg swelled with pustules, and his foot also, and it came to destruction.
Therefore I was called to him: and I hurried to untying the bandage: and peace followed, and he escaped from his pains.
But corruption had already been confirmed in the member, and I was not able to restrain it.
So then the corruption ceased to move through the member, until it perished.
And I saw another doctor who pierced a cancerous abscess: and it became ulcerated after days, until the evil grew great with his lord.
That is, because when the cancer is pure from a melancholic humor, then it should not be reached with iron altogether, unless it is in a limb that can tolerate it, so that the whole of it may be cut off.
And because of that O' Father's, it is necessary for you to know that the operation with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, an operation which is associated with health, and an operation with which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already marked in every place of this book, where the operation comes, in which there is fear and trembling.
Wherefore it is necessary for you to beware of that and depart from it, so that foolish people may not find the way to talking about it and dishonoring it.
Therefore take the measure with solicitude and protection, and care for your patients with facility and firmness, and use the better way leading through God's grace to salvation and a praiseworthy succession: and dismiss terrible afflictions difficult of healing: and take your souls away from that which makes you fear, so that doubt may not enter upon you in your faith and advantage.
For indeed it remains more for your glory, and higher in this world, and finally to your profit.
Galenus has indeed said in some of his own warnings. You will not cure the bad affliction: do not call yourselves evil physicians.
However, I have now divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
The First Chapter.
On Caustic with fire, and Caustic with sharp medicine, divided, and ordered from head to feet, and forms of instruments, and tools of the cauter, and all that is necessary in the operation.
The Second Chapter.
On incision and perforation, bloodletting and purging, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and similar things to that: and all divided and ordered according to forms of instruments.

On the restoration and reduction of displacements and torsions, and similar things: a chapter ordered from head to feet, and forms of instruments.
But first of all, before I remember the operation with him, it is necessary that I say what are his qualities and harms of cautery, and in which complexion he should be shown.
I therefore say that the word about the quality of cautery and its harms is a long and subtle discourse, knowledge and a hidden secret.
And many wise people have spoken about it and disagreed on the matter; and for me indeed enough is said from their words, fearing lengthening.
I therefore say that cautery is applied universally to every complexion, which is with matter and without matter: excepting the two complexions, which are hot complexion without matter and dry complexion without matter.
But in the hot and dry complexion with matter they disagreed. For some said that cautery is beneficial in it. And others said the opposite of that, namely that cautery is not suitable in a disease which is from heat and dryness: because the nature of fire is heat: and it is improper for one to be healed from a hot and dry disease with something hot and dry.
And he who says the opposite said that through cautery a benefit is made in every hot and dry disease which occurs in the bodies of men: because when you compare the body of man and his humors to the complexion of fire, you find the body of man to be cold.
And I myself say by his words: because experience has already revealed it to me on several occasions.
However it is not necessary that he should come over this unless he who has already been tested and exercised in the exercise of cautery, and knows the diversity of human complexions, and the disposition of illnesses within themselves, and their causes, and accidents, and the span of time for them.
But from the other complexions there is no fear over you, and especially in cold and moist illnesses. For indeed all physicians have agreed on these and have not disagreed with Cautery in treating them.
And know, sons, that from the secret of treatment by Cautery with fire and its goodness over Cautery with burning medicine is this: because fire is simple, whose action does not reach, unless to the member that is cauterized, and it does no harm to another connected member with it, unless a small damage.
The action of burning medicine indeed reaches to that which is removed from the members, and perhaps it causes an accident in a member, a difficult-to-heal illness, and perhaps it kills.
But fire because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance does not do that, unless there is an excess.
And indeed this has become clear to us through experience, because of the length of service and study with art, and standing on the truth of things, and because of that I excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not so, because this is not permitted in my book, I would have brought you the secret that is hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies of expulsion, by which it expels illnesses with a philosophical speech demonstrated to your minds.
And know, sons, that they themselves disagree about the time in which it is suitable to make a cautery, and place better the true time.
And I say that a cautery is suitable at all times: therefore, because an injury occurring due to the passage of time is submerged in healing, which is drawn with a cautery. And especially if the cautery is for pains from necessary, strong, and grievous pains which do not tolerate delay: therefore it is feared that a more serious harm will occur than the slight injury that passes with time.
And may it not fall into your minds, oh sons, that which the common people and foolish doctors do not think, namely that the affliction that is cured by a cautery does not always recover: and they put forth this consequence, and the thing is not as they think: therefore a cautery is not, except in place of medicine, which alters the complexion, and dries up the humors that are causes why pains occur.
However, a cautery is useless on top of medicine because of the speed and effectiveness of its own health and the power of its operation and the intensity of its dominion: and it is possible that the affliction returns an hour or some time later according to the complexion of the sick man and the location of his affliction and the strength of it: and what is prepared in his body from the aggregation of excesses within him: and which comes to him in its acquisition from foods and similar things from causes, unless the affliction occurs where the cautery is administered.
A subtle affliction in a few excesses and humors of a member, such as tooth ache from a cautery on the teeth, and similar to these, it is possible that the pain will not return in that place. But this happens in only a few cases.
But the common people's speech again, that a cautery is last resort of medicine, is true: not for what they intend by it: because they believe that there is no cure which comes with medicine, nor with any other after the cautery has been applied.
However, it seems you forgot to provide the text. Please paste the Latin text from the medieval translation of Albucasis' textbook on surgery, and I'll translate it into English for you.
The antiqui said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron. And they did not say this, unless because of the equality and subtlety of its substance. And they said that a place does not become suppurated from the cautery. But that is not absolutely true; for I have already tested it and found that it does not do this in some bodies without doing so in others.
And cautery with it is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you put the cautery made from gold into fire, it is not clear to you what quantity of fire you are using because of the redness of the gold: and when it hastens towards cold, and if you add more heat on top of it, it melts in the fire and turns into plates.
Therefore, the craftsman falls short of it in terms of the task: and because of this, cautery with iron becomes quicker and more convenient for us than with gold, in accordance with righteousness to the operation.
And for my part I have already arranged this chapter on Cautery according to chapters and have arranged it from head to foot so that the seeker may easily find what he wants in it.
Chapter 2.
Cauterization here corrects the lordship of moisture and coldness over the brain, which are causes of headaches and the multitude of fluxes of fluids from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and the multitude of sleepiness and toothache and throat pain: and in general all afflictions that occur due to coldness, such as paralysis and epilepsy and apoplexy and similar ones from those afflictions.
The method of cauterization is as follows: you should first administer to the ailing person medicine in liquid form that purifies the head for three nights, or four, according to the strength of the ailing person and their age and habit.
Then order him to shave his head with a razor. Then have him sit between your hands square, so that he has already put his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm over the root of his nose in between his eyes. Therefore wherever your middle finger has reached, mark that spot with caustic.
Then ignite the cautery oil mixture, whose form is this.
Then place it over the marked spot with caustic, descending as you gradually turn your hand, so that it is drawn back. Then quickly withdraw your hand and look at the place.
And if you see that already a quantity has been revealed from the bone of the head, or a quantity of flesh, then withdraw your hand. And if not, repeat your hand with the iron itself, or with another from it when it has cooled, until the bones that I told you of are visible.
Then take some salt, dissolve it in water, and soak a cloth in it, and place it over the spot: and leave it for three days.
Then place a cloth that has been soaked in butter over it, and leave it on the spot until the burn's scab is destroyed. Then take care of it with the ointment of four medicines, until it heals.
They have said that as much as the wound remains more open, it emits pus: therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them have said that the skin should be cauterized all the way to the bone: and the cautery should be held until something of the thickness of a bone is burnt.
Then it is carved out of bone after what has been burnt, then it is treated.
And others say that it is necessary to reach the end with a cautery until it imprints on the bone an impression like the form of a small cauldron: or else the instrument that women place on an infusion of small alphabet letters. And they suppose that vapors are exhaled from this place of the head, and the open wound is left for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it consolidates.
But to me they do not seem altogether to be a cauterizing of this kind, except perhaps in some men according to the course of fear.
And leaving it alone, I think it is better for its own safety.
For the head is weakened by the dissolution of its own natural continuity, just as we have testified in other limbs, and especially when a weak and feeble person's head is involved. Indeed, I think that first kind of cauterizing is safer and better for me, and I use it: so let us proceed with this in order to heal.
Chapter 3.
When there is a long-standing pain throughout the entire head of an invalid, and he has used honey, and mustard, and vinegar, and oils, and poultices. And especially if it has already been cauterized with the first cautery that we have narrated, and it does not bring any relief to him: then consider. For if the head of an invalid is strong and robust by nature, not feeble, and finds a severe coldness: then cauterize it with another cautery slightly below. Then cauterize it above every horn of his own head with a cautery, but let it not pass through the skin, and uncover the quantity which we have narrated from the bone. And cauterize him with a cautery one on the back of his head, at a place which is called "the jug": and it is the place where poultice is put: and lift up your mother in this way, and do not make an incision in the mouth. For indeed he finds pain there because of it, a violent pain, and different from the pain of other cauterizations on the head of all.
And I will say that this cautery is in its place: and it must be a cautery by which the horns of the head are cauterized, and his occiput more subtly with a cautery by which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When the pain happens in one part of the head and swelling, or when the pain spreads as far as to the eye, and the head is cleaned with purifying medicines, and the rest of the treatment which I said in the divisions of infirmities is administered, and that does not cure it all: then the cauterization in it is according to two manners: either cauterization with burning medicine: or with iron.
The cautery with burning medicine is, as you take one tooth of garlic, and scrape off its skin, and cut off the ends from two sides. Then split the place of pain with a wide lancet until it is under the skin where the tooth takes hold.
So put it into the place under the skin until it is hidden: then bind a cloth tightly over it with a suitable constriction, and leave it for fifteen hours, then dissolve it and take out the garlic, and let the ulcer remain two days or three: afterwards put a linen cloth soaked in butter on top of it until the place becomes pus: then cure it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to do that with certain medicines inflaming, which I wrote in the twelfth book, on Inflaming Medicines.
His cauterization with iron is done in this way. Fire caustic, whose shape is this.
And it is called Clavus because its shape resembles the shape of a key, wherein there is something curved and in the middle thereof is a small prominence.
Then place it on the spot and hold your hand back; and you turn the iron gradually with speed; and let the quantity that is inflamed be half of its thickness. And raise your hand, so that the artery below does not become inflamed and a flow of blood occurs.
Then soak the cotton in salt water and place it on the spot, and let it be for three days; then put the cotton with butter upon it; afterwards cure it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicrania with the second part of the cutting instrument of caustic. And beware of an incision into the artery in this hemicrania, lest it become inflamed properly.
On the manner of cauterizing in ancient hemicrania.
When you treat hemicrania, with what we said from the preceding cure, and what we said in the divisions of pains, and the treatment does not bring relief: and you see from the pain, that it is not sufficient for him whom we mentioned by the first cauter with medicine, or with cauter with fire, then it is necessary to use the iron caustic knife, until it whitens after you mark on the spot of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger's length, or rather that: and put your hand in place one time, and bind it until you cut the artery, and come up to the bone.
However it is necessary for you to be careful about the continuity of the jawbone, which moves during mastication, lest the side or the nerve that moves it becomes irritated, and thus spasms occur.
And be on guard and take care also to prevent the flow of blood from the cut artery. For indeed there is fear in cutting it, and especially for one who does not know what he is doing, nor is diligent or experienced, and leaves the operation as his first priority.
And I come back with a reminder of the rule for regulating the flow of blood that has occurred from an artery according to its own manner and in its proper place in this book.
But if you see from the illness that this cautery is not sufficient for him, and you see that the body of a weak person tolerates a cautery in the middle of the head, as we have narrated, take care of the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, administer the cautery which we said to be used in the chapter on extracting an artery with a cautery having two knives. For indeed this cautery is better and more beneficial.
On the manner of cauterizing an earache.
When a pain occurs in the ear from cold and is treated with liniments and the rest of the treatment which we said to be divided, but the pain does not depart, then use a caustic fire and it is that which is called Point, whose form is this.
Then make points with it around the ear after its ignition all around, as it turns over; or around both ears at once if there is pain in both. And extend yourself with the caustic a little from the root of the ear after you have marked the places with cerate; and let the quantity of the caustic be ten points all around each ear, and so on.
Then cure the place until they are healed.
About the way of cauterizing in a torture device.
Chapter 7.
A torture that is cured with cauterization is nothing other than from kinds of afflictions which occur due to phlegm, according to what we said about divisions of illnesses.
And it is suitable for cauterizing the species that occurs from dryness and spasm of the nerve.
When you cure this kind of torture with herbs, and poultices, and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and a second little lower than its place, and a third at the conjunction of the two lips.
And place your cauterization on the opposite side of the weak part. Because softening does not occur unless in the part that appears to be healthy.
And the shape of the cautery is that you cauterize it with a cautery on the direct end of the upper ear extremity below the horn of the head, and another at its time, whose length is according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until it burns a quantity of the middle thickness of the skin.
And this is the shape of the cautery, and it is a kind of knife, whose form was mentioned before: however it is not finer than little, as you see: and it must be a knife with a little excess thickness.
Then cure the place, with what preceded, until it heals.
About the way of cauterizing in Old Apoplexy.
When the old apoplexy is stirred up and you cure it with what we said, and your treatment does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries over all of his head's horn, and a cautery in the middle of the head, as we mentioned, and a cautery on the back of the head, according to what preceded: and the manner of the cautery is according to what preceded.
Even cautery is applied with a cautery over the mouth of the stomach: and it is the most extreme.
Then it is to be scraped, with that which preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in the drink they be given first to the ailing person hawthorn of great quantity and cleansing pills for the brain.
Then shave the head of the ailing person completely and place on the back of his head a plaster of pine resin described in the treatise on plasters, and put it on him several times.
For indeed that is the manner of cautery: and make it according to the same order which I said there.
If therefore he be healed by that, well. If not, then make three cauteries on the back of his head, which are descending from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye, and place between every cautery a thickness of a finger.
Then care for the cautery, with that which preceded it.
But if you wish to add an additional one, and he is a patient suffering from it: then make a cautery in the middle. And if you wish to add another, then cautery him over both horns.
Then take care of him until he be healed; and let the cautery be with oil according to the form which was said before.
About the manner of cautering for paralysis and relaxation.
Chapter X.
It is necessary that you proceed in cleansing the head with hawthorn and with what we said before.
Then shave the head of the ailing person: afterwards cautery him with a cautery on the middle of his head, and a cautery over every horn of his head, and a cautery on the back of it, and three on the vertebrae of his neck.
If however you are in a condition of softening the body by many things, and he is infirm and weak, and the suffering is strong: then cautery him with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and the last with cautery, until it burns much from his skin, and lift up your hand. Then cure him, until he be healed; and thus anoint the cautery with oil.
Concerning the manner of cautering in epilepsy.
An epileptic is not to be cauterized, unless it be the one whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
It is therefore necessary that you cleanse his brain with rue first, and with the rest of the cure which we said in the division: when he is very weak, or tolerates not well the taking of medicines.
But if he is a child, who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargling and purifying chewing of the brain is administered to him, for many days before that with a bettering of food.
Then scrape his head after, then cautery him with one cautery in the middle of his head, following as it preceded in manner: and another cautery on the back of his head, and over all his ear cauldrum with a cautery. But if he is weak yet strong, and tolerates well, then cautery him with the cauteries which I said for one having paralysis, and softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck, and vertebrae of the back: and let the cautery be anointed with oil according to the manner which preceded.
But if he is a weak child, then put a subtle cautery on him, in this manner.
Concerning the manner of cautering in melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cautery him with the cauteries which we said for one having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an abundance of bile leading to melancholy, and the body of the ailing person is humid, then give him a drink that will purify his brain, according to what was said in division: then rub the head of the ailing person and make afterwards a bandage well made from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of his head: and let the ailing person sitting upright be held by all parts.
Then apply an ointment. And it is more suitable from the butter of old sheep. And warm him over moderate heat on fire with a temperature measure that a finger can endure when inserted into it. Then empty it out from the middle of his head into a circle, and let him go until he cools down.
Make this for the ailing person once every week, with his other good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cautery him by making many small points on him, except that you hold your hand with the cautery: and let it smell.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with quality.
Then place over it a cloth soaked in butter or hen's fat.
A method of cautering descending to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When the principle of water is declared to you in the eye through signs, as I said in division, then begin and drink the ailing person with that which purifies his head.
And guard him from all humidity, and make him sit in a bath on empty days for several days.
Then order him to rub his head and cautery himself in the middle of his head. Then cautery him above both temples with two cauteries, if there is an onset of water descending in both eyes at once: or from one side, if there is an onset of water in one eye: and cut out with a cautery all veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in breadth over the temples: and beware of blood flow.
If you see something from it, then cut him off immediately with any medicine that is possible: and I come away with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and cutting them, and taking care against bleeding.
And sometimes he is cauterized on the neck, under two bones, with two blisters produced at the end.
On the manner of cauterizing in old tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and constant: and they are over veins, and arteries which are manifestly on the outside of the head, it is verified that this is from cold and phlegmatic excesses: then cauterize with a cautery same as I narrated in the incision of descending water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two blisters above two temples, and two blisters on the neck under two bones. And if you need an increase, then cauterize him on every side of the eye carefully, over the extremity of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
On the manner of cauterizing in a foul odor of the nose.
When you are treating him with that which we said in the division, and the treatment does not agree: then hasten, and give him infirmocochias to drink for three nights: then scrape his head, and cauterize him with a middle cautery, with an oil-bearing cautery. Then cauterize him with a key cautery two times, on the two eyebrows under the hair a little.
And be careful of the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of a key cautery.
On the manner of cauterizing in softening the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye becomes softened by illness or moisture: then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with this moon-shaped cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize him above the eyebrows a little with two cauteries in each part; and lengthen them from both eyelashes: and let the length of all the cauterie be according to the lengths of the eyebrow; and do not finish your hand with the cauterie, nay, according to what is scorched one third of the eyelid.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs are inverted and pierce the eye.
The cautery in that case is according to two modes: either a fire-cautery, or a burning medicine-cautery.
But in the fire-cautery, first order the patient to pluck out his hairs beforehand, if he has those which clean them, until they are lengthened and conformed. But if they pierce him at the root: then bind his eyes with a strip of cloth so that they may not be moved until they grow again.
So when they grow and conform, then place the patient's head in your bosom; afterwards mark above his eyelid with wax, a mark shaped like a myrtle leaf, and let its beginning be near the hairs.
Then place a poultice soaked in egg-white: or on mullein sap over the eye.
Then make a cautery with fire, whose shape is this.
Then cauterize over the figure you marked slowly in many stages, until the surface of the skin is completely burned, appearing like a proper shaped leaf of myrtle.
And the sign of the work's health is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted, and the hairs raised at the point of the eye.
Therefore lift up your hand then, and let him go for three days.
Then place over it a cloth with butter, until the scab is eradicated. Then care for him with ointment, until he heals.
But if some hair comes back again after an hour and the eyelid becomes soft: then repeat cauterization over that place, just as you did at first.
But if the hairs are in the lower part [of the eyelid]: then cauterize it, until it is raised to its natural place; and it will be equal so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is so that you may instruct the patient to remove the hairs until they are prolonged and equalized. Make from cloth a shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap and from unimbued chalk each a weight of one ounce or almost that amount; then mix them together with good grinding and make it quickly so that it does not become cold. Then spread a piece from it over the cloth which you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over the eyelid of one eye or two. And place under the eye a cloth soaked in egg white; and the head of the patient be in your bosom.
And place your index finger over the medicine, and press it slightly. And you move it whenever the patient feels a stinging of the medicine, for the sting finds its way like fire.
While therefore this which he himself feels a stinging continues, then remove the medicine and move it with your finger. When therefore the stinging quiets down, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And then consider if you see the eyelid raised, like when it is contracted with fire or with an incision, it is well; and if not, then repeat over it from the medicine above the place in which the medicine did not penetrate nor become darkened, until your operation is equalized and the eye is constricted.
Then place over it a compress with butter until the burnt skin is scraped away. Then treat him with a transparent ointment, or another, until he heals.
And it is necessary for you to take care during the operation that nothing from the medicine falls into his eye.
But if the eyelid becomes soft after a day and something gets into his eye from his hair, then repeat the medicine over that place which has become soft from the eyelid properly, just as you did at first. Then treat him until he heals.
And this is the form of a myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness. Therefore according to this, let your consideration be: and justice is not hidden from him who has zeal for this art.
About the way of cauterizing a tear duct fistula.
When you treat the fistula, with what we said about the suffering and your treatment does not bring relief: then it is necessary that you cauterize it itself in this way.
Order the sick person to place his head in your arm and hold his head with one hand so that it may not be moved or shaken with his own head.
Then place the infused cataplasm on his eyelid or on the mucus of the plant silphium over his eye; then with a fire cauterizer in this form.
Let it be concave, like the form of a vulture's feather quill at one end, with which the cauterizer is made: and if you wish it to be penetrating up to the other extremity, and if you wish it to be thus stretched upwards.
However this concavity is better for your task.
Then express the fistula if it is open and draw out from it pus and dry it up; and if it is not open, then open it and drain its pus.
Then place upon it a cauterizer, which is made very hot.
And hold your hand near the cauterizer with the eye, up to the nose, so that your hand does not stray or bother the patient; and place the cauterizer on the eyelid fat and corrupt it.
If then you reach to the beginning of your cauterizer up to the mouth, it will be good. And if not, then repeat the cauterizer once or twice as you need to; and leave it for three days.
Then place a compress with butter on it, and care for the eye with a drying ointment until it heals.
But if forty days pass and it does not heal: then place on it a sharp corroding medicine until the eye socket is uncovered; and scrape it according to what comes up in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some of the first said. Pay attention to the place of the fistula and find it; then place in it a thin caming, that is, a thin cannula, whose shape is this. And pour into it a quantity of drachma of molten lead, and hold your hand with good cannula retention, and the patient must not be moved at all, so that he does not run or reach the molten lead to his eye.
And it is necessary to place on the eye of the patient a compress soaked in egg white or in water.
For lead burns the place of the fistula and heals it with a wondrous healing.
Which if the fistula is healed, along with what we said from the cauterizing and the cure, it is good. And if not, then necessity is that you administer a nostril hole and lead the fistula back to its natural course, according to what comes up to its own place.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing in clefts of the lips.
Fissures frequently occur in the lip which are called clefts, and most especially in the lips of boys.
When therefore you treat these clefts as we said in the division of diseases, and treatment does not help, then with a small burning iron cuteler, according to this shape.
And let its concavity be according to the subtlety of the knife.
Then place the burning iron hastily into the clefts themselves, until the cautery reaches the depth of the clefts.
Then treat it with ceruse, until it heals.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing a fistula of the mouth.
When an apostema occurs at the root of a tooth, or on the palate, or at the roots of teeth: then it makes pus and bursts: afterwards it becomes inflamed and runs with pus and forms a fistula: then you treat this and treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you prepare a burning cautery according to its size so as to enter into the fistula. Then insert the burning iron into the opening of the fistula and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches its depth and last part: do that once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards with what we said concerning treatment until it is healed.
If therefore the discharge is cut out and heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to lay open the place and remove the corrupted bone according to what will come into its head.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing in softened gums and teeth.
When the gums are softened because of moisture and the teeth are loose and you treat them with medicines and it does not help: then place the head of the patient in your armpit.
Next, a cauterization by fire, the form of which will appear after this. Place a cannula over the tooth and insert into it a burning cautery quickly. And hold your hand for a brief moment until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
And lift up your hand: then reinsert the cautery a few times, as you wish.
Then the patient should fill his mouth with salt water and hold it for one hour and then spit it out.
For the tooth is strengthened by movement, and the inflamed gum is tightened and the corrupted moisture dries up.
About the manner of cauterizing for pain of the teeth.
When the pain of the tooth is because of coldness, either there is chill within it or a worm, and treatment does not bring relief with medicines, then a cautery is applied to it in two ways: either a cautery with butter or a cautery by fire.
The cautery with butter is, that you take sour butter and boil it in a metal or earthenware pot. Then take a cloth and wrap it around the end of the cautery. Then immerse it in the boiling butter and place it on the painful tooth quickly, and hold it until it cools down; then reinsert it a few times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse a cloth or rag in cold butter and place it on the painful tooth; then place a hot iron over it until the fire reaches the depth of the cavity of the tooth.
The cauterization with fire is, that you take a metal or iron air cannula. And there should be something thickness within his body so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the sick person.
Then take a cautery by fire, whose shape will come; and place it on that tooth; and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do this several times, for the pain will be driven away, either on that same day or on another day.
And it is necessary that during the pressure of that cautery, the sick person fills his mouth with good beeswax and holds it for one hour; then he spits it out.
And this is the shape of the cautery.
Apply cauterization with whatever extremity you wish according to what is possible; and this is the shape of the cannula.
On the manner of cauterizing in fistulas.
When fistulas are from phlegm and from cold moistures, and they do not obey digestion by means of medications, and you wish to hasten their digestion: then take a concave cautery by fire, whose shape is this.
Having two open extremities, so that smoke can issue from the other end of the cautery; and place it lit over the fistula once, and a second time if you need to, until it reaches the depth of the fistula.
But if the fistula is small, then place the cautery according to the size of the fistula.
Then leave it for three days, and place a warm poultice on it in butter until what was burned by the fire is removed.
Then care for it with tooth ointment, until it heals to its natural shape of a cannula.
On the manner of cauterizing in hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When moistures cling to the trachea and particularly when it is with coldness of complexion, then it is necessary that the sick person be purged first with dissolvent medications.
Then cauterize him at the back of the throat near the root of the tongue in a depressed place. And beware lest you come too close with the cautery to the throat, nor to the skin, except a little of it.
Then cauterize him with another cautery at the junction of the neck in the last vertebra, ending it. And let the cautery be a nail-shape, as was done before.
Then cure him with that which came before, until he is healed.
Of the manner of cauterizing for diseases of the Lung and Cough.
When cough and disease of the lung are from cold humors and the patient is not fevered nor consumptive, nor long suffering: then cauterize him with two cauteries above the armpit in depressed, gentle, vacant places. And another cautery on the middle of the chest between the two breasts; and let the cautery be a tube-shape, as was done before.
And if you wish your cautery to be a piercing with the instrument called "Punctum", whose shape was shown before in the piercing of ear pain, and let there be points from thirty points until it reaches to others.
Then cure him with that which came before, until he is healed.
And now let the cautery be one having three branches, according to this shape. Why is it alleviated with that cautery, when you do with it instead of one, three cauteries.
Chapter XXVII.
When the arm is dislocated because of humidities and does not return to its place in an hour from being dislocated, until it becomes his habit of returning, then is dislocated by a small movement which happens as we have already proved that, you must first reduce the dislocation. Then the patient shall be placed on his back, or on a healthy side. Then lift the scalp, which is in the inner part of the skull to the top with the fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated to the inside.
Then take a cauterizing iron having two horns. Whose shape is this.
Then cauterize the scalp until it penetrates to the other side, and the figure of the cauterizing will come with four horns.
And sometimes a cauterization is done with an iron having three horns, therefore the figure of the cauterizing then becomes six horn-like projections: and the horns are tested for fineness.
And this is the shape of the cauterizing iron having three horns.
And sometimes one more is added in this manner, therefore there are eight cauterizers.
Then place over the cauterizing iron crushed thorns with salt. Then make the patient calm down, so that the member does not move at any time until it is comforted.
And if the dislocation is to the top, and it rarely happens, then cauterize it on the shoulder with a key-shaped cauterizer, or with many-pointed cauterizers.
For the joint is strengthened and moisture is removed, and the patient becomes healthy.
¶ On how to cauterize the Stomach.
When coldness and much moisture occur in the stomach until they draw it out of its complexion, and multiply phlegm to it, and frequent methods of treatment do not help: then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back, and extend his legs and hands. Then cauterize with three cauterizers: the cauterizer under the earlobe of the size of one finger with the key-shaped cauterizer, and two cauterizers lower down from both sides each one cauterizer, until the figure of the horns becomes triangular. And lengthen it between both so that they are not joined together, when they make a discharge.
And let the depth of the cautery be the quantity of two thirds of the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of the cauteries be according to this shape without addition; and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach, according to this shape: and let the cautery by which this cautery is made be one according to the figure of a circle, according to this shape.
And the stomach is cauterized by piercing it with that which is irritated by this cautery; and it is, as signs are marked on the stomach in the quantity you wish with encaustic: then cauterize him with a cautery of a point: then heal him with the treatment that preceded until he is healed.
Of the manner of cauterizing the spleen, cold.
When the pain occurs in the spleen from coldness and moisture, or from thick phlegm, until it goes out of its natural complexion with a superfluous discharge, and the sick person is cured with what we said, but it does not benefit them: then it is necessary that the sick person be laid on their back on their own neck, and signs be marked with encaustic three cauteries according to this shape, and this quantity the same over the spleen below the hips, where the man's knee reaches; and let the space between every cautery be according to the thickness of a finger; and let the cautery be straight according to the length of the body; and do not press your hand with the cautery too much.
And let the quantity of what is burned be according to the thickness of the skin, half of that without addition; and let the sick person stand on their own feet.
But if he is not standing, then let him lie down, who has already extended his legs and lifted up his arms.
This is the form of a cautery.
And indeed it is possible for you to cauterize with this cautery and a surgical knife, when you have fineness and prudence in the art.
And take care that you do not finally proceed with the cauterization, and the thickness of the skin is completely burned, so that the whole body is burned and comes to the intestines: for the skin there is thin, therefore you know this.
On the manner of cauterizing boils on the liver.
When an issue occurs and you wish to know if it is a boil on the liver itself or on its covering: then if it is on the liver itself, it invades the patient with severe pain and weight without sharpness: and if it is on the covering of the liver, with pain there is sharpness and vehemence: and already you see that its treatment has wearied his physicians.
Therefore it is necessary for the patient to lean back over their own head. Then mark the place of the boil with resin, then apply a burning cautery that resembles a rod. And this is its form. And cauterize with it a single cautery until the skin is burned completely and comes to the spleen, until all the pus issues forth: then cure the issue with the treatment of issues, until it heals.
And it is not necessary for this type of cautery to be used, except by one whose study in the art of medicine extends long, and through whose hands those afflictions come with some experience: then indeed let them dare to perform such an operation.
But rather to leave it alone, for me it is better.
On the manner of cauterizing in pleurisy.
The ancients said that a cautery with the roots of Aristolochia should be used for cold pleurisy in this manner. And take from the roots of long, dry aristolochia one root longer than those which are found in it, and as thick as the thumb. Then immerse it in oil and set it on fire. Then cauterize with a cautery one in the place between the fork of the neck and the collarbone, and two small cauterizations somewhat inclined downwards towards the part that is under the beard.
And two small cauterizations also in the place between the fifth and sixth ribs inclined downwards towards the back a little; and another cautery in the middle of the chest and one above the stomach. And three cauterizations from behind: one in the place that is between two spades; and two small cauterizations from both sides of the chest, with the lower one being in the place that is between two spades.
And it should not be necessary for you to compress your hand with the cautery, rather let it be visible and emitting a skin-smelling odor.
And some old ones have said that there are men who use a cautery of iron similar to a reed and set it on fire, and then insert it into the place between the ribs until they reach the boil and pus issues forth: just as we said concerning the boil of Epatic.
But in this piercing with a cautery there is danger, that either the sick person dies immediately or a fistula occurs in the place which does not have healing.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the Spleen Chapter XXXII.
When you are treating the pain of the spleen, with what we said concerning treatment in the division of pains, and your treatment does not take effect, then a cautery is applied to it in three modes, all of which are straight.
One of these is that you make three cauterizations, or four lined ones along the length of the spleen according to the figure of the cauteries of Epaticus, whose figure precedes this one.
And let it be between all cautery a quantity of finger thickness, or more or less.
And let the mode of cautery be what we have said to be used for cauterizing the liver equally.
And do not compress your hand with the cautery, and let the patient lie supine on his back.
And another mode of cautery is: that you have a fire cautery with two horns, as we said in the chapter on dislocation of the arm; and lift up the skin which is over the spleen directly where the left elbow of the patient reaches; and let your elevation be according to the breadth of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then insert two very hot horns into the patient, until with them you pierce the skin on one side; then withdraw the cautery; thus four cauteries are formed.
And if you wish to cauterize with a cautery having three horns.
Then take care of the cautery after you let it discharge pus for many days, since it is more beneficial than any remaining thing that has preceded in treatment.
Of the mode of cauterizing in dropsy.
The cautery does not fall in dropsy, unless it is properly applied.
When you are treating dropsy with the modes of cure which we said in the division, and the treatment does not confer, then it is necessary that you cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and one over the stomach, and another over the spleen, and two behind the spine, and one directly on the chest, and another directly on the stomach: and let the quantity of depth of the cautery be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the open cautery so that it may discharge pus for a long time.
And they should not exclude an ailing person from treatment after cautery, for it is necessary that two intentions concur with him, and healing will hasten to him with the aid of God.
The form of cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be a iron spike, according to its own form, and that with which the back is cauterized, an olive-shaped one, according to its own form.
On the manner of cautering feet and legs.
When they become suppurated and are filled with greenish water, it is necessary to cautery over the dorsum of the foot in the notch, which is between the auricular and annular bones; and lift your hand with the cautery and do not twist it: then lift your hand and repeat this absolutely not.
For greenish water will flow out, and the cautery should be according to this shape.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and the cautery with a cutting-point cautery should be made; and one cautery should be made according to the length of the leg, one under the knee, and another lower down near the middle of the leg; and above all the hip two cauteries: and leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time, so that some water may flow out from it; then treat him with the rest which we said.
On the manner of cautering in resolving an intestinal obstruction.
Chapter 35.
When there is a resolution of the intestines from coldness and dampness, until the vital and digestive powers, which are in the stomach and intestines, become weakened, and it is cured with modes of treatment but does not get well: and you see the patient bearing a cautery of great virtue, then cauterize him with a large cautery over his stomach, according to what was done in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery, and four small cauteries around the navel with a thin iron spike cautery, and a large cautery over the groin above the hip or two cauteries.
And if you see excessive moistures, and the patient endures them, then burn him with a cautery on the chest, and with a cautery over the whole hip: and perhaps add two small cauteries near the great belly.
For it is a good treatment, whose benefit does not err.
About the method of burning hemorrhoids.
Chapter 36.
When there are old and many hemorrhoids, or one, which are thick with cold humors or corrupted moistures, and are treated as we said in the division, and the treatment does not avail: then burn him with three cauteries on the lower part of the back of the spine near the scapula a little triangularly, and with a cautery under the navel almost two fingers deep.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled and his food is not digested, and you see his face become inflamed, then burn him on the stomach with a large cautery, in the manner described before: and on his liver and another on his spleen with a key-shaped cautery: and leave the cautery open for some time: then care for him until he is healed.
Chapter 37.
When you cut out the hemorrhoids, then ignite a cautery resembling a reed. Then insert the ignited cautery into the cut out hemorrhoid, and with your last hand guide it until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which the blood flows: do this once or twice.
If therefore there are many hemorrhoids, then burn each one with a cautery according to what we have narrated. Then care for them, with that which you apply to them from ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize him with a large cautery on the scrotum, it is more extreme in treatment.
On the manner of cauterizing fistulas in the anus.
Chapter Thirty-eight.
When the sick person does not obey surgery and the operation which we have described in its place, and is frightened by it, perhaps he will be healed with a cautery.
When therefore an abscess occurs to someone, and suppurates, the pus flows out from it, and corrupted humors are discharged. Therefore what is necessary and fitting is that you probe her with a thin reed. Then know the depth of it with the reed.
Then ignite the cautery, which is similar to a rod. Then insert yourself into it ignited inside the fistula and to the depth in which the rod has entered.
And iterate over it the cautery, until all the corrupted bodies are burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to your necessity.
And take care to avoid burning the nerve, if there is one there, or a large vein; or if the fistula goes into the body of the bladder, or into the body of the intestine; then be careful about all those places.
And do not do that unless the fistula is in a fleshy place and you think it is not penetrating.
Then take care of the place until it heals.
But if the place is sealed and material has been cut away from it, and remains so for a long time: then you will know that it is now completely healed.
And if material does not dry out from it, then you will know that it is penetrating, or there is a corrupted bone in its depth, or something like those: whose remembrance will come to the place itself.
On the manner of cauterizing kidneys.
When there occurs a pain in the kidneys due to cold or from a thick congestion and it is diminished because of the patient's weakened constitution, then it is necessary that you cauterize it on alum over the kidneys, with a caustic on the entire kidney along with a key-shaped caustic, whose preparation has been previously mentioned.
And perhaps we shall cauterize it again on the alum itself. Why three lines will come. So they will be more beneficial for healing.
On the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening of the bladder occur from cold and moistures, until the infirm person is unable to retain urine, then you shall cauterize it in the lower part of the abdomen over the bladder, where the pubic hairs begin, and with a caustic on the right side of the abdomen and another on the left; and let the length of this cauterization be according to the size of a thumb's knuckle: and you shall cauterize it with an inferior dorsal caustic, or with two caustics, if need be; and in accordance with what preceded, use a key-shaped caustic.
On the method of cauterizing the uterus.
When coldness and moistures occur in the uterus, and are prevented from conception because of it, and its menses become corrupted, and their coming is delayed, and she suffers pain at their arrival, then it is necessary that three caustics be placed around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and a caustic on the lower back below the loin, or two caustics: and let the key-shaped caustic be used.
On the method of applying a cauter to an Achlam in case of dislocation.
When the mucous humors are discharged to the Achlam and it is caused to be expelled from its place; and the sign of this is that the crus extends over the other when they are placed together: and the location of the dislocation is found in the empty space.
Therefore it is necessary that you cauterize the ailing part over the Achlam itself with a similar cauter circle: after you have marked with encaustic around the edge of the Achlam, as it turns round: and so that the Achlam itself falls in the middle of the circle.
But if this cautery is not present to you, then cauterize the Achlam with three cauteries, using a large oil cautery: and let the depth of the cautery be according to the quantity of thickness of the skin of the whole.
Then care for it until it is healed.
On the method of applying a cauter to sciatica.
When pain occurs in the Achlam and coldness and humors are its cause: and the patient is treated as we said in the division, and the cure does not come about and it worsens: then it is necessary that you remove the ailing part from thick humors with stinking pills, or with artificial pills, and similar things. Then cauterize him.
And the method of applying a cauter to it is according to two modes: either a cautery with burning medicines, or a cautery with fire.
A cautery with fire is in accordance with many methods.
One of them is to cauterize above the Achlam itself with three triangular cauteries, according to this shape. And make a depth good, or bad in them. And let the space be what is between every caustic of the thickness of a finger, and let the caustic be oily.
However when it happens that a caustic is put in the middle over the top of the head itself. Why are there four caustics.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded in the cauterizing of dislocations also, one: that it may be a circle containing the whole head.
And burn the thickness of the skin entirely.
This is the method of cauterizing sciatica, when the pain adheres to itself and does not extend as far as the hip and thigh.
But if it extends as far as the hip and thigh, then you will cauterize it with two caustics over the hip, over the place where the ailing person points there, in which is the pain, and burn your caustic on the hair of four fingers to the western part for a little while: and let the caustic be a knife-like one.
And let the depth of the caustic be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
But if the ailing person indicates that the pain extends as far as almost to the fingers of the foot, then you will cauterize it there where he indicates with a pointed caustic, three or four, or more if needed.
And if he indicates that the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, then you will cauterize it there with a knife-like caustic.
And beware of you in every cauterization of yours, that you do not burn with a caustic to this extent so as to burn the nerve, or a large artery, and bring evil or harm through it upon the sick person, or a contraction.
And indeed I have seen one or the other of those who cauterized over the hair and went too far in the cauterization, and it has become swollen with a tumor that reached the foot, and it was perforated and entirely corrupted: then there followed a dissolution of the belly, and death after this.
If there is pain in two places at once, cauterize both in this manner.
And some wise men have said that even a barber can do cauterizing, with this method of cautery being his way. Make a similar iron spatula with a diameter of half a fist: and let it be at its mouth according to the thickness of a thumb nail, or slightly less: and within that spatula let there be another spatula.
And let the space be between each spatula equal to the thickness of a thumb knot: and let the spatulas be open on both sides: and let their height be as a knot, or two knots: and make for them a handle from iron well suited to the spatulas.
Then it should be heated in the fire until it reddens and spits out sparks: then it is to be put over the barber's cauldron, beside a patient lying on their healthy side. Therefore cauterize him with three round cauteries in turn one after another.
Then leave it alone for three days. Afterwards, apply ointments with butter and let the open wound remain many days. Then cure him with a balm until he is healed.
Albucasis says, we have been sparingly using this kind of cautery, because of the terror of its appearance, and therefore that few are found who endure it.
However it is a good cautery for one who endures it and finds a suitable place with it.
However the cautery with medicines set on fire is like this: you make two spatulas having a ring-shaped hole, into which descends the hinge of its door from iron or air, the length of a wall: and let the height of them be as two knots, or just so.
And let the space between both be equal in thickness to a finger, and they are open below and above: and it is so that they contain themselves together, according to this form.
Then place it upon a chest with a lid, an invalid lying on his back on a sound side. And compress your hand very much over the chest with a lid. Then pour between the two circles water that is warmed a little with fire, and hold it for the space of one hour; and let the invalid endure its burning and scalding, for he finds the burning as if it were fire, until the burning ceases.
Then raise your hand with the instrument and wipe away the warm water from the chest entirely with fresh water; then let it be for three days.
And place on it butter, until the blackening of the scalding is removed; and let it be for some days, and pus will come out from it. For indeed it is a remedy for the last stage.
Then care for it with ointments until it heals.
But if the pain extends as far as the hip or thigh, make for him a statue in it that contains water, according to what you did on the chest equally.
And this is the method of hot water: and I have already written it in the treatise on the correction of medical treatments. Take alkali and burnt lime, both equal in quantity, one part of each; pound them well, and put them in a new pot, the lower part of which is pierced with a small hole, according to the size that will allow water to flow through it: and put under the bottom of the pot another unglazed pot: and pour over the alkali and lime fresh water, which will cover both by a finger's breadth: after which you compress them well with your hand in good compression; and leave the pot until the sharp water descends into the lower part of the unglazed pot.
Then gather all that water and pour it over another lime; and let it settle until it clears again.
Then it will be very sharp and keen, which is administered in many medical operations, and in the cauterizing of other members. Because it brings about the operation of its own fire.
And there are medicines with which joints can be cauterized, even as the thistle, and honey of a nut called acharium, and limestone with soap, so that both are mixed together.
And Galen himself reported telling of the cure of a certain man from among the ancients, by which he was cured of the pain in his joints and the vein of Sciatica; and he highly praised its being very great. And he said that he did not need another cure, and that he was cured in one instance, until he reported this, because perhaps he himself had entered the bath carried, and had come out of it already healed.
And it is to be taken from the green sap of the seitarag plant; and if it cannot be found green, dry but fresh is taken: and it is rubbed well with a bit of fat, and placed over the joint where there is pain, or the leg, or in the hip: and it is bound on, and left for a period of three hours, or until the sick person feels relief from the burning. Then put him into the bath.
When therefore sweat breaks out on his body, put him onto a couch. For the pain departs and he is healed.
And know that it is not right for anyone to use a cautery with these medicines, unless after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides also said that goat dung, when it is used to cautery the vein of Sciatica, cures him; and it makes a cautery in this manner. There is taken wool and it is steeped in old oil, and it is put over the deep place, which is between the big toe and the ankle bone, and it is closer to the ankle bone.
Then take dried sheep dung and ignite it until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on wool and leave it until it is extinguished. Then repeat the process. So do not stop doing this until a feeling of warmth reaches as far as the navel and the pain is quieted.
And that method of cautery is called calx (or) Vaccinum.
Of the cautery of pain of the back.
And sometimes a pain occurs on the back from many causes, or by chance, or from a blow, or from an excessive discharge, and similar things, due to the infusion of cold and moist matter: and in this case indeed cautery does not fall unless in this single form, which is made from the infusion of cold matter.
Therefore after the discharge of the patient with pills made from foul-smelling things and similar ones to be placed on the back where there is pain, three lines according to the width of that part should be drawn, after signs have been marked with encaustic in each line five cauteries or more as much as the strength of the patient tolerates: and a cauterization should be done with cauterizing points.
And if you want, cauterize three or four times with a middle-sized cautery stick, in this form.
Of the manner of cauterizing in the beginning of swelling.
This affliction often occurs in small children.
And the sign of its beginning is that it occurs on them as a swelling above the breathing at elevation and movement: and in the last vertebrae of the back and their knots, which already begin to protrude over the other vertebrae.
When therefore you see it and want to do this, then cauterize it with a cautery that is a circle in this form.
And he should take the cauterizing iron over the entire back part of the spine equally: and if you wish to cauterize around the spine with the cauterizing iron, two or three points, making sure they are close together.
Then cure the place, until it heals along with what we said.
And beware that you do not administer caustic to a hump that forms due to a spasm of the nerve.
Of the method of cauterizing for Gout, and pains of joints.
When the pains of the joints are from cold and damp humors that flow to any part of the body, then when these pains occur in the feet, it is customary for physicians to call that Gout properly.
Therefore, when Gout caused by cold is cured with the methods of treatment and the pains are not removed, then cauterization removes them.
And it is to cauterize him after evacuation around the joint of the feet with many cauteries and that the caustic be olive.
And if you wish to make points on the surface of the foot, then do so with a pointy caustic. But if the pains ascend as far as the knees, or to other joints, and it often happens that way, then cauterize him over the entire knee with three cauteries, or four from every part, with the same caustic of Clavus.
But if you need to use more of this caustic, then cauterize him again. And do not immerse your hand in the caustic, rather it should be so thick as the thickness of the skin.
But if the pains ascend to the knees and the back, then administer what we said from the caustic in Chapter its own.
But if the pains are only in the hands, then make points around the fingers, as two lines turn.
If, however, there remains pain from wounds in fingers, then prick them with a needle over every swelling, and over the wrist of the hand.
If, however, the pains ascend after days to the elbows or to the shoulders, then cauterize both sides from all parts.
And do not discharge the sick person from good regime, from receiving medicines. For if a good regime is done, and the mucus is discharged, with God's help the patient will be cured with this cauterization.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing for ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, and descends into the intestines or the scrotum to the testicle, and it is beginning to come near: then it behoves you to command the patient to abstain from food on its day. And let him use gentle remedies, so that dung may descend from his belly.
Then have him sit between your hands on his back: and command him to hold his breath, until it issues out, or the scrotum or intestines become apparent.
Then reduce it into place with your fingers, and mark with encaustum below the rupture over the opening of the scrotum, with a sign whose extremity is similar to half a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then burn with fire a cautery of this form, until white, and it spits out sparks. Then reduce the intestines or scrotum to its natural position. Then have the attendant place his hand on the place, so that the intestines do not come out: and you have already opened between the patient's thighs, and placed under him a mattress, and another servant above his knees, and another above his chest who is holding his hands.
Then place the cautery on top of it, with your hand standing straight with the cautery. And hold him fast until you reach with him the mouth: or go on with him another time, if you are not successful with him at first up to the mouth.
And carefully observe from the exit of the intestines at the time of your cauterisation, lest you burn it and a bad event happens through that on the patient, or death, or great harm.
And know that when you are not successful with the cautery in reaching the mouth, your operation is not beneficial.
And it should be a slender cautery for children, according to their size.
Then care for him with the other ointments until he is healed.
And let the patient be lying on his back for forty days, until the wound is covered.
And it should be that you put his food according to the length of time of his cure, so that it relieves his belly: lest he go out with diarrhea and vomiting.
Then when he wants to rise after forty days, then administer a well-made bandage and keep him for forty other days.
And he should be spared from labor, and filling with food and drink, and violent speech.
For when he uses this regimen, thus is he healed with whole healing.
And I say the cure of Ruptures with incision in his chapter.
When however the Ruptures occur in the rest of the belly and are beginning to be, and you wish not for them to become worse, then cauterize his rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let that which is burnt from then on be like a third part of it. Then care for him, as we have said, and he will not become worse.
And some of the first said that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, in this shape.
After it is signed with wax and a line is placed which is through the width on the upper side of the rupture and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with a key cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
About the way of cauterizing for pains from a fall, or blow.
Chapter 48.
When it happens to some members from a fall or blow, and the pain persists for a long time, and care does not improve with medicines; then it is necessary that they be cauterized with a puncture cautery.
And let the cautery be of every member according to its size and weakness, and its smallness, and its weakness, and its power, and the location of the twisting and pain from it.
Therefore if it is healed from the first cautery, that is good. If not, then repeat on it a second cautery.
Because of the habit of these pains is to change from member to that which approaches it. Therefore you must pursue them with a cautery until the sick one is healed.
About the way of cauterizing for Leprosy.
The lepers however are sometimes relieved by cautery with great relief. And especially the kind of leprosy which occurs because of the corruption of phlegm and melancholy; so when you wish to cauterize it, consider this.
If therefore the leprosy is beginning and you have cured it with what we said in division, and it does not descend nor remain; and you fear for the sick one that corruption will encompass his whole complexion: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries; one in the middle of the head marked, and a second below that towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two above both horns, and one behind on the back of the neck.
And with the last of your hands and a cautery, touch it for a little while until it impresses on the bone a small impression, and the outer coatings are dislodged from it; so that the exhalation of thick vapors from it may be alleviated, and cauterize also with a cautery over the spleen itself, according to what has gone before.
But if the leprosy has already spread over the infirm person and appears manifestly: then it is necessary that he be cauterized with those cauteries which we said in the head, and one on the tip of the nose, and two on the cheeks, and two on the vertebrae of the neck, and six on the vertebrae of the back, and a large one above the joints of the tail and another above it, at the almeidati: and two on the flanks: namely one on the entire flank, and two on the knees: one on the entire knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the calves, and two on the tendernesses of his chest: and he should be cauterized over the entire junction, from the joints of his hands and feet, and he should be cauterized on the entire heel of his feet, and the palms of his hands.
And take care that you do not burn the nerves which are over the posterior part of the heel.
And when he is cauterized with a cautery on the breastbone, and another on the ribcage, and another on the liver.
And know that as much as you add a cautery is so much more beneficial, and so much more helpful.
And know that the infirm person does not find pain in the cautery as those who are healthy do: therefore his body is already numb.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of great size and smallness according to the members and joints: according to what preceded from the kinds of instruments.
Then cure the cautery with flour of the herb with honey, and the rest of the care, until it heals.
A chapter about how to cauterize in a stupor.
When some member is numb and is cured with medicines, and oils, and plasters, and does not heal, then cauterize the numb member with cauteries, according to what its magnitude or smallness deserves.
And let your cautery be inserted a little way into the thickness of the skin. Then care for it with an ointment until it heals.
And sometimes it is cauteryed for a numbness which occurs to the hand and foot, in the vertebrae of the back near the exit of the nerves that move that limb; and the numbness is removed.
But one should not presume to do it over that, unless he is wise about the anatomy of limbs and the exit of nerves moving the body.
Chapter 51.
When the elbow becomes inflamed and does not yield to anything from the arts of medicine: then cautery it with a deep cautery a little way, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its colour changes.
Then care for it with flour of herb, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and the blood of a dove, and the blood of a hyrundine: each one part of these things; they are mixed together and applied to the place on a cloth, until it heals.
About the manner of cautering in a Cancer.
When the cancer is beginning and you wish to suppress it: then cautery it with a circular cautery around its circumference, as it rotates.
But wise men have said that it should be cauteryed with the last cautery in the middle.
But to me it does not seem so, for I fear that it will ulcereate, and I have already seen it so a few times.
And it is more correct to cautery it around its circumference with a circle, as we said, or with many cauteries.
About the manner of cautering on an Ulcer.
When someone has a wound and is delayed in healing because of an excess of fluid forming in it, or because the person is elderly and of poor blood, or because of time, and wishing to hasten the healing of the wound, then cauterize around its edges with many small punctures from cauteries. Then let him leave it alone. For itself will hasten with healing.
If however you wish to puncture it with a cautery, then make a fire cautery, the shape of which is this.
And place it in the middle of the wound until it penetrates the skin; and let the cautery be from that which follows the sick part, so that it may ease the flow of pus.
Then care for it until it heals.
About the manner of cauterizing a corrupting ulcer.
Chapter 52.
A corroding ulcer is nothing but corruption of a walking member and it consumes the member itself: just as fire devours dry wood.
If therefore you see a corroding ulcer in a place which can tolerate the cautery with fire, then burn it with much fire, small and large caustics, according to what is fitting for that place where the corroding ulcer is.
Then cauterize it from every part until you eradicate all corruption and nothing remains of it altogether.
Then let it be for three days, and put over the areas that have been cauterized a pounded sulfur with oil until all scabs are eradicated and all corruption.
Then care for it with ointments producing flesh.
If therefore you see that after three days the flesh grows back healthy and uncorrupted, it is good.
And if not, then repeat the cautery over what remains of the corrupted places.
And the corroding ulcer is healed sometimes with sharp medicine. The wound itself rises in place of the cautery.
However, a cautery with fire is more speedy relief and I have already said that the cauterizing of it with sharp medicine is in a division; therefore take it there when you need it.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing on Clavus and Verrucae.
Chapter 55.
This suffering often occurs in the lower parts of the feet and is a thick, lumpy, filtered thing that hurts the foot.
And indeed there are two manners of cautery for it: a cautery with fire and a cautery with hot water.
But as much as it is with fire, that the fiery cautery be conch-shaped like a vulture's feather: which shall be made of iron, according to the quantity that contains a nail on all sides and has thin edges.
Then place it burning on the clavus. Then turn the hand with the cautery around the clavus until the cautery reaches the depth of the clavus: and let it be for three days until it begins to emit pus. Then apply a plaster to it with wild mallows crushed with salt: and let the plaster stay on it at night. For indeed it will be rooted out from its roots.
Then care for the place with a unguent that generates flesh until it heals.
But if they are not converted and often occur on the surface of the body, especially in hands and feet: then administer to them a cautery with hot water: and it is, as you should take a tube from air or iron or from a vulture's feather: and place it over the clavus or althelul.
